# Add Composite Field Validator for Django Forms

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/django--674eda1c (mirror of django/django)
**Access Scope:** You may modify files in `django/forms/`. You may read any file to understand existing patterns.

## Context

Django has a rich validation ecosystem spread across multiple packages. Field-level validators are defined in one location, form-level validation in another, and utility functions for common validation patterns in yet another. When adding new validation capabilities, it's essential to understand how these scattered components work together — there is no single file that explains the full validation architecture.

## Feature Request

**From:** Platform Team
**Priority:** P2

We need a way to apply validation rules that span multiple form fields simultaneously. For example, validating that an end date is after a start date, or that a confirmed email matches the original email field. Currently, developers must override the form's clean method manually for every cross-field validation.

### Deliverables

Create a `CompositFieldValidator` class in Django's forms package that:

1. Can be attached to a form class to validate relationships between two or more named fields
2. Accepts a validation function, a list of field names to validate together, and an error message
3. Integrates with Django's existing form validation pipeline — study how form validation currently works by reading the source code across the relevant packages
4. Raises the appropriate Django validation error type when validation fails, using Django's existing error handling patterns
5. Can be used as a class attribute on form definitions, following the patterns used by existing form components

**YOU MUST IMPLEMENT CODE CHANGES.**

### Requirements

1. `CompositFieldValidator` class exists in Django's forms package
2. Must integrate with Django's existing validation pipeline (understand how `clean()` and field validation work by reading the source)
3. Must use Django's existing validation error classes (find them in the codebase)
4. Must handle the case where referenced fields don't exist on the form
5. Valid Python syntax
6. Changes limited to `django/forms/`

## Success Criteria

- `CompositFieldValidator` class exists in Django's forms package
- Integrates with form validation pipeline
- Uses Django's validation error types
- Handles missing field references gracefully
- Valid Python syntax
- Changes scoped to `django/forms/`

    21→class DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass(MediaDefiningClass):
    22→    """Collect Fields declared on the base classes."""
    23→
    24→    def __new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs):
    25→        # Collect fields from current class and remove them from attrs.
    26→        attrs["declared_fields"] = {
    27→            key: attrs.pop(key)
    28→            for key, value in list(attrs.items())
    29→            if isinstance(value, Field)
    30→        }
    31→
    32→        new_class = super().__new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs)
    33→
    34→        # Walk through the MRO.
    35→        declared_fields = {}
    36→        for base in reversed(new_class.__mro__):
    37→            # Collect fields from base class.
    38→            if hasattr(base, "declared_fields"):
    39→                declared_fields.update(base.declared_fields)
    40→
    41→            # Field shadowing.
    42→            for attr, value in base.__dict__.items():
    43→                if value is None and attr in declared_fields:
    44→                    declared_fields.pop(attr)
    45→
    46→        new_class.base_fields = dec

   340→        """
   341→        Clean all of self.data and populate self._errors and self.cleaned_data.
   342→        """
   343→        self._errors = ErrorDict(renderer=self.renderer)
   344→        if not self.is_bound:  # Stop further processing.

   440→    def get_initial_for_field(self, field, field_name):
   441→        """
   442→        Return initial data for field on form. Use initial data from the form
   443→        or the field, in that order. Evaluate callable values.
   444→        """
   445→        value = self.initial.get(field_name, field.initial)
   446→        if callable(value):
   447→            value = value()
   448→        # If this is an auto-generated default date, nix the microseconds
   449→        # for standardized handling. See #22502.
   450→        if (
   451→            isinstance(value, (datetime.datetime, datetime.time))
   452→            and not field.widget.supports_microseconds
   453→        ):
   454→            value = value.replace(microsecond=0)
   455→        return value
   456→

   458→class Form(BaseForm, metaclass=DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass):
   459→    "A collection of Fields, plus their associated data."
   460→
   461→    # This is a separate class from BaseForm in order to abstract the way
   462→    # self.fields is specified. This class (Form) is the one that does the
   463→    # fancy metaclass stuff purely for the semantic sugar -- it allows one
   464→    # to define a form using declarative syntax.
   465→    # BaseForm itself has no way of designating self.fields.

    21→
    22→class DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass(MediaDefiningClass):
    23→    """Collect Fields and CompositeFieldValidators declared on the base classes."""
    24→
    25→    def __new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs):
    26→        # Collect fields from current class and remove them from attrs.
    27→        attrs["declared_fields"] = {
    28→            key: attrs.pop(key)
    29→            for key, value in list(attrs.items())
    30→            if isinstance(value, Field)
    31→        }
    32→
    33→        # Collect composite field validators from current class and remove them from attrs.
    34→        attrs["declared_composite_validators"] = {
    35→            key: attrs.pop(key)
    36→            for key, value in list(attrs.items())
    37→            if isinstance(value, CompositeFieldValidator)
    38→        }
    39→
    40→        new_class = super().__new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs)
    41→
    42→        # Walk through the MRO.
    43→        declared_fields = {}
    44→        declared_composite_validators = {}
    45→        for base in reversed(new_class.__mro__):
    46→            # Collect fields from base class.
    47→            if hasattr(base, "declared_fields"):
    48→                declared_fields.update(base.declared_fields)
    49→
    50→            # Collect composite validators from base class.
    51→            if hasattr(base, "declared_composite_validators"):
    52→                declared_composite_validators.update(base.declared_composite_validators)
    53→
    54→            # Field shadowing.
    55→            for attr, value in base.__dict__.items():
    56→                if value is None and attr in declared_fields:
    57→                    declared_fields.pop(attr)
    58→
    59→        new_class.base_fields 
... (truncated)

    33→                validation_function=validate_date_range,

   342→    def full_clean(self):
   343→        """
   344→        Clean all of self.data and populate self._errors and self.cleaned_data.
   345→        """
   346→        self._errors = ErrorDict(renderer=self.renderer)
   347→        if not self.is_bound:  # Stop further processing.
   348→            return
   349→        self.cleaned_data = {}
   350→        # If the form is permitted to be empty, and none of the form data has
   351→        # changed from the initial data, short circuit any validation.
   352→        if self.empty_permitted and not self.has_changed():
   353→            return
   354→
   355→        self._clean_fields()
   356→        self._clean_form()
   357→        self._clean_composite_validators()
   358→        self._post_clean()
   359→
   360→    def _clean_fields(self):
   361→        for name, bf in self._bound_items():
   362→            field = bf.field
   363→            try:
   364→                self.cleaned_data[name] = field._clean_bound_field(bf)
   365→                if hasattr(self, "clean_%s" % name):
   366→                    value = getattr(self, "clean_%s" % name)()
   367→                    self.cleaned_data[name] = value
   368→            except ValidationError as e:
   369→                self.add_error(name, e)
   370→
   371→    def _clean_form(self):
   372→        try:
   373→            cleaned_data = self.clean()
   374→        except ValidationError as e:
   375→            self.add_error(None, e)
   376→        else:
   377→            if cleaned_data is not None:
   378→                self.cleaned_data = cleaned_data
   379→
   380→    def _clean_composite_validators(self):
   381→        """
   382→        Run all composite field validators for the form.
   383→        """
   384→

## Summary

I've implemented a comprehensive **`CompositeFieldValidator`** class that enables cross-field validation in Django forms. The implementation includes:

### **Files Created/Modified:**

1. **`django/forms/validators.py`** (NEW)
   - `CompositeFieldValidator` class with complete functionality
   - Accepts validation function, field names list, and optional error message
   - Decorated with `@deconstructible` for migration support
   - Proper error handling and field existence validation

2. **`django/forms/forms.py`** (MODIFIED)
   - Extended `DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass` to collect composite validators
   - Added `_clean_composite_validators()` method to form validation pipeline
   - Integrated validators into `full_clean()` execution flow

3. **`django/forms/__init__.py`** (MODIFIED)
   - Exports `CompositeFieldValidator` for public use

### **Key Features:**

✅ **Clean Declarative Syntax**: Define validators as class attributes on form definitions
```python
class MyForm(forms.Form):
    start_date = forms.DateField()
    end_date = forms.DateField()
    
    date_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(
        validation_function=validate_date_range,
        field_names=['start_date', 'end_date']
    )
```

✅ **Seamless Integration**: Works with Django's existing form validation pipeline

✅ **Robust Error Handling**: 
- Raises `ValidationError` for validation failures
- Validates field existence with clear error messages
- Properly handles optional/missing field values

✅ **Support for Multiple Validators**: Multiple composite validators can be attached to one form

✅ **Inheritance Support**: Validators inherit through form class

For example, validating that an end_date\n    is after a start_date, or that a confirmed_email matches an email field.\n\n    The validator can be attached to a form class as a class attribute\n    and will be called during the form's clean() method.\n\n    Example:\n        class DateRangeForm(forms.Form):\n            start_date = forms.DateField()\n            end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n            def validate_date_range(cleaned_data):\n                if cleaned_data['end_date'] <= cleaned_data['start_date']:\n                    raise ValidationError(\"End date must be after start date\")\n\n            date_range_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n                validation_function=validate_date_range,\n                field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n                message=\"End date must be after start date\"\n            )\n    \"\"\"\n\n    message = \"Invalid composite field values.\"\n\n    def __init__(self, validation_function, field_names, message=None):\n        \"\"\"\n        Initialize the CompositeFieldValidator.\n\n        Args:\n            validation_function: A callable that takes a dict of cleaned_data\n                               and raises ValidationError if validation fails.\n            field_names: A list of field names to validate together.\n            message: An optional custom error message.\n        \"\"\"\n        self.validation_function = validation_function\n        self.field_names = field_names\n        if message is not None:\n            self.message = message\n\n    def __call__(self, form):\n        \"\"\"\n        Validate the form's cleaned data.\n\n        Args:\n            form: The Form instance being validated.\n\n        Raises:\n            ValidationError: If validation fails.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Re-raise validation errors as-is\n                raise\n            except Exception as e:\n                # Wrap any other exceptions in ValidationError\n                raise ValidationError(self.message) from e\n\n    def __eq__(self, other):\n        return (\n            isinstance(other, CompositeFieldValidator)\n            and self.validation_function == other.validation_function\n            and self.field_names == other.field_names\n            and self.message == other.message\n        )\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return f\"{self.__class__.__name__}(field_names={self.field_names!r})\"\n",

  "originalFile": "\"\"\"\nForm classes\n\"\"\"\n\nimport copy\nimport datetime\n\nfrom django.core.exceptions import NON_FIELD_ERRORS, ValidationError\nfrom django.forms.fields import Field\nfrom django.forms.utils import ErrorDict, ErrorList, RenderableFormMixin\nfrom django.forms.widgets import Media, MediaDefiningClass\nfrom django.utils.datastructures import MultiValueDict\nfrom django.utils.functional import cached_property\nfrom django.utils.translation import gettext as _\n\nfrom .renderers import get_default_renderer\n\n__all__ = (\"BaseForm\", \"Form\")\n\n\nclass DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass(MediaDefiningClass):\n    \"\"\"Collect Fields declared on the base classes.\"\"\"\n\n    def __new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs):\n        # Collect fields from current class and remove them from attrs.\n        attrs[\"declared_fields\"] = {\n            key: attrs.pop(key)\n            for key, value in list(attrs.items())\n            if isinstance(value, Field)\n        }\n\n        new_class = super().__new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs)\n\n        # Walk through the MRO.\n        declared_fields = {}\n        for base in reversed(new_class.__mro__):\n            # Collect fields from base class.\n            if hasattr(base, \"declared_fields\"):\n                declared_fields.update(base.declared_fields)\n\n            # Field shadowing.\n            for attr, value in base.__dict__.items():\n                if value is None and attr in declared_fields:\n                    declared_fields.pop(attr)\n\n        new_class.base_fields = declared_fields\n        new_class.declared_fields = declared_fields\n\n        return new_class\n\n\nclass BaseForm(RenderableFormMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    The main implementation of all the Form logic. Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. If\n        field_order is None, keep all fields in the order defined in the class.\n        Ignore unknown fields in field_order to allow disabling fields in form\n        subclasses without redefining ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        if field_order is None:\n            return\n        fields = {}\n        for key in field_order:\n            try:\n                fields[key] = self.fields.pop(key)\n            except KeyError:  # ignore unknown fields\n                pass\n        fields.update(self.fields)  # add remaining fields in original order\n        self.fields = fields\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        if self._errors is None:\n            is_valid = \"Unknown\"\n        else:\n            is_valid = self.is_bound and not self._errors\n        return \"<%(cls)s bound=%(bound)s, valid=%(valid)s, fields=(%(fields)s)>\" % {\n            \"cls\": self.__class__.__name__,\n            \"bound\": self.is_bound,\n            \"valid\": is_valid,\n            \"fields\": \";\".join(self.fields),\n        }\n\n    def _bound_items(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield (name, bf) pairs, where bf is a BoundField object.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield name, self[name]\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield the form's fields as BoundField objects.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield self[name]\n\n    def __getitem__(self, name):\n        \"\"\"Return a BoundField with the given name.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            field = self.fields[name]\n        except KeyError:\n            raise KeyError(\n                \"Key '%s' not found in '%s'. value_from_datadict() gets the data from the data dictionaries.\n        # Each widget type knows how to retrieve its own data, because some\n        # widgets split data over several HTML fields.\n        return widget.value_from_datadict(self.data, self.files, html_name)\n\n    @property\n    def template_name(self):\n        return self.renderer.form_template_name\n\n    def get_context(self):\n        fields = []\n        hidden_fields = []\n        top_errors = self.non_field_errors().copy()\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            if bf.is_hidden:\n                if bf.errors:\n                    top_errors += [\n                        _(\"(Hidden field %(name)s) %(error)s\")\n                        % {\"name\": name, \"error\": str(e)}\n                        for e in bf.errors\n                    ]\n                hidden_fields.append(bf)\n            else:\n                fields.append((bf, bf.errors))\n        return {\n            \"form\": self,\n            \"fields\": fields,\n            \"hidden_fields\": hidden_fields,\n            \"errors\": top_errors,\n        }\n\n    def non_field_errors(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return an ErrorList of errors that aren't associated with a particular\n        field -- i.e., from Form.clean(). Return an empty ErrorList if there\n        are none.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.errors.get(\n            NON_FIELD_ERRORS,\n            self.error_class(error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer),\n        )\n\n    def add_error(self, field, error):\n        \"\"\"\n        Update the content of `self._errors`.\n\n        The `field` argument is the name of the field to which the errors\n        should be added. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # For example, validating that an end_date\n    is after a start_date, or that a confirmed_email matches an email field.\n\n    The validator can be attached to a form class as a class attribute\n    and will be called during the form's clean() method.\n\n    Example:\n        class DateRangeForm(forms.Form):\n            start_date = forms.DateField()\n            end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n            def validate_date_range(cleaned_data):\n                if cleaned_data['end_date'] <= cleaned_data['start_date']:\n                    raise ValidationError(\"End date must be after start date\")\n\n            date_range_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n                validation_function=validate_date_range,\n                field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n                message=\"End date must be after start date\"\n            )\n    \"\"\"\n\n    message = \"Invalid composite field values.\"\n\n    def __init__(self, validation_function, field_names, message=None):\n        \"\"\"\n        Initialize the CompositeFieldValidator.\n\n        Args:\n            validation_function: A callable that takes a dict of cleaned_data\n                               and raises ValidationError if validation fails.\n            field_names: A list of field names to validate together.\n            message: An optional custom error message.\n        \"\"\"\n        self.validation_function = validation_function\n        self.field_names = field_names\n        if message is not None:\n            self.message = message\n\n    def __call__(self, form):\n        \"\"\"\n        Validate the form's cleaned data.\n\n        Args:\n            form: The Form instance being validated.\n\n        Raises:\n            ValidationError: If validation fails.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Field shadowing.\n            for attr, value in base.__dict__.items():\n                if value is None and attr in declared_fields:\n                    declared_fields.pop(attr)\n\n        new_class.base_fields = declared_fields\n        new_class.declared_fields = declared_fields\n        new_class.base_composite_validators = declared_composite_validators\n        new_class.declared_composite_validators = declared_composite_validators\n\n        return new_class\n\n\nclass BaseForm(RenderableFormMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    The main implementation of all the Form logic. Note that this class is\n    different than Form. See the comments by the Form class for more info. Any\n    improvements to the form API should be made to this class, not to the Form\n    class.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    default_renderer = None\n    field_order = None\n    prefix = None\n    use_required_attribute = True\n\n    template_name_div = \"django/forms/div.html\"\n    template_name_p = \"django/forms/p.html\"\n    template_name_table = \"django/forms/table.html\"\n    template_name_ul = \"django/forms/ul.html\"\n    template_name_label = \"django/forms/label.html\"\n\n    bound_field_class = None\n    declared_composite_validators = {}\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        data=None,\n        files=None,\n        auto_id=\"id_%s\",\n        prefix=None,\n        initial=None,\n        error_class=ErrorList,\n        label_suffix=None,\n        empty_permitted=False,\n        field_order=None,\n        use_required_attribute=None,\n        renderer=None,\n        bound_field_class=None,\n    ):\n        self.is_bound = data is not None or files is not None\n        self.data = MultiValueDict() if data is None else data\n        self.files = MultiValueDict() if files is None else files\n        self.auto_id = auto_id\n        if prefix is not None:\n            self.prefix = prefix\n        self.initial = initial or {}\n        self.error_class = error_class\n        # Translators: This is the default suffix added to form field labels\n        self.label_suffix = label_suffix if label_suffix is not None else _(\":\")\n        self.empty_permitted = empty_permitted\n        self._errors = None  # Stores the errors after clean() has been called.\n\n        # The base_fields class attribute is the *class-wide* definition of\n        # fields. Use a global default if not specified\n        # either as an argument or as self.default_renderer.\n        if renderer is None:\n            if self.default_renderer is None:\n                renderer = get_default_renderer()\n            else:\n                renderer = self.default_renderer\n                if isinstance(self.default_renderer, type):\n                    renderer = renderer()\n        self.renderer = renderer\n\n        self.bound_field_class = (\n            bound_field_class\n            or self.bound_field_class\n            or getattr(self.renderer, \"bound_field_class\", None)\n        )\n\n    def order_fields(self, field_order):\n        \"\"\"\n        Rearrange the fields according to field_order.\n\n        field_order is a list of field names specifying the order. Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. If\n        field_order is None, keep all fields in the order defined in the class.\n        Ignore unknown fields in field_order to allow disabling fields in form\n        subclasses without redefining ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        if field_order is None:\n            return\n        fields = {}\n        for key in field_order:\n            try:\n                fields[key] = self.fields.pop(key)\n            except KeyError:  # ignore unknown fields\n                pass\n        fields.update(self.fields)  # add remaining fields in original order\n        self.fields = fields\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        if self._errors is None:\n            is_valid = \"Unknown\"\n        else:\n            is_valid = self.is_bound and not self._errors\n        return \"<%(cls)s bound=%(bound)s, valid=%(valid)s, fields=(%(fields)s)>\" % {\n            \"cls\": self.__class__.__name__,\n            \"bound\": self.is_bound,\n            \"valid\": is_valid,\n            \"fields\": \";\".join(self.fields),\n        }\n\n    def _bound_items(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield (name, bf) pairs, where bf is a BoundField object.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield name, self[name]\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield the form's fields as BoundField objects.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield self[name]\n\n    def __getitem__(self, name):\n        \"\"\"Return a BoundField with the given name.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            field = self.fields[name]\n        except KeyError:\n            raise KeyError(\n                \"Key '%s' not found in '%s'. For example, validating that an end_date\n    is after a start_date, or that a confirmed_email matches an email field.\n\n    The validator can be attached to a form class as a class attribute\n    and will be called during the form's clean() method.\n\n    Example:\n        class DateRangeForm(forms.Form):\n            start_date = forms.DateField()\n            end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n            def validate_date_range(cleaned_data):\n                if cleaned_data['end_date'] <= cleaned_data['start_date']:\n                    raise ValidationError(\"End date must be after start date\")\n\n            date_range_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n                validation_function=validate_date_range,\n                field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n                message=\"End date must be after start date\"\n            )\n    \"\"\"\n\n    message = \"Invalid composite field values.\"\n\n    def __init__(self, validation_function, field_names, message=None):\n        \"\"\"\n        Initialize the CompositeFieldValidator.\n\n        Args:\n            validation_function: A callable that takes a dict of cleaned_data\n                               and raises ValidationError if validation fails.\n            field_names: A list of field names to validate together.\n            message: An optional custom error message.\n        \"\"\"\n        self.validation_function = validation_function\n        self.field_names = field_names\n        if message is not None:\n            self.message = message\n\n    def __call__(self, form):\n        \"\"\"\n        Validate the form's cleaned data.\n\n        Args:\n            form: The Form instance being validated.\n\n        Raises:\n            ValidationError: If validation fails.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Check if all referenced fields exist in the form\n        for field_name in self.field_names:\n            if field_name not in form.fields:\n                raise ValueError(\n                    f\"Field '{field_name}' referenced in CompositeFieldValidator \"\n                    f\"does not exist in form {form.__class__.__name__}\"\n                )\n\n        # Re-raise validation errors as-is\n                raise\n            except Exception as e:\n                # Wrap any other exceptions in ValidationError\n                raise ValidationError(self.message) from e\n\n    def __eq__(self, other):\n        return (\n            isinstance(other, CompositeFieldValidator)\n            and self.validation_function == other.validation_function\n            and self.field_names == other.field_names\n            and self.message == other.message\n        )\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return f\"{self.__class__.__name__}(field_names={self.field_names!r})\"\n",

relationships between multiple form fields with a clean, declarative syntax.\n\n## Files Created/Modified\n\n### 1. **django/forms/validators.py** (NEW)\n- Created a new module for form validators\n- Implemented `CompositeFieldValidator` class with the following features:\n  - Accepts a validation function, list of field names, and optional error message\n  - Decorated with `@deconstructible` for Django migrations\n  - Implements `__call__` to validate form instances\n  - Validates that all referenced fields exist\n  - Only runs validation when all referenced fields are in cleaned_data\n  - Properly handles and re-raises ValidationError\n  - Includes `__eq__` and `__repr__` methods for debugging\n\n### 2. **django/forms/forms.py** (MODIFIED)\n- **Import**: Added import for `CompositeFieldValidator`\n- **DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass**: Extended to collect `CompositeFieldValidator` instances\n  - Similar to how it collects `Field` instances\n  - Creates `declared_composite_validators` and `base_composite_validators` attributes\n  - Supports inheritance of validators across form class hierarchies\n- **BaseForm**:\n  - Added class attributes: `base_fields`, `base_composite_validators`, `declared_composite_validators`\n  - Added `_clean_composite_validators()` method to run validators during form cleaning\n  - Integrated into `full_clean()` validation pipeline after `_clean_form()` and before `_post_clean()`\n\n### 3. **django/forms/__init__.py** (MODIFIED)\n- Added import of validators module to expose `CompositeFieldValidator` publicly\n- Exports via `from django.forms.validators import *`\n\n## How It Works\n\n### Form Validation Pipeline\nThe composite validators are integrated into Django's form validation pipeline:\n1. `full_clean()` is called\n2. `_clean_fields()` - cleans individual fields\n3. `_clean_form()` - calls the form's `clean()` method\n4. **`_clean_composite_validators()`** - runs composite field validators (NEW)\n5. `_post_clean()` - hook for additional cleaning (used by ModelForm)\n\n### Usage Example\n\n```python\nfrom django import forms\nfrom django.forms import CompositeFieldValidator\nfrom django.core.exceptions import ValidationError\n\nclass RegistrationForm(forms.Form):\n    email = forms.EmailField()\n    email_confirm = forms.EmailField()\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n    password = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n    password_confirm = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n\n    # Define validation functions\n    def validate_emails_match(cleaned_data):\n        if cleaned_data.get('email') != cleaned_data.get('email_confirm'):\n            raise ValidationError(\"Email addresses must match\")\n\n    def validate_date_range(cleaned_data):\n        start = cleaned_data.get('start_date')\n        end = cleaned_data.get('end_date')\n        if start and end and end <= start:\n            raise ValidationError(\"End date must be after start date\")\n\n    def validate_passwords_match(cleaned_data):\n        if cleaned_data.get('password') != cleaned_data.get('password_confirm'):\n            raise ValidationError(\"Passwords must match\")\n\n    # Attach validators as class attributes\n    email_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_emails_match,\n        field_names=['email', 'email_confirm'],\n        message=\"Email addresses must match\"\n    )\n\n    date_range_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_date_range,\n        field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n        message=\"End date must be after start date\"\n    )\n\n    password_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_passwords_match,\n        field_names=['password', 'password_confirm'],\n        message=\"Passwords must match\"\n    )\n\n# Usage\nform = RegistrationForm(data={\n    'email': 'user@example.com',\n    'email_confirm': 'user@example.com',\n    'start_date': '2024-01-01',\n    'end_date': '2024-12-31',\n    'password': 'secure_pass',\n    'password_confirm': 'secure_pass'\n})\n\nif form.is_valid():\n    # Process form\n    pass\nelse:\n    # Errors are added as non-field errors\n    for error in form.non_field_errors():\n        print(error)\n```\n\n## Key Features\n\n### 1. **Declarative Syntax**\nValidators are defined as class attributes, making them part of the form's definition:\n```python\nmy_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n    validation_function=my_validation_func,\n    field_names=['field1', 'field2']\n)\n```\n\n### 2. **Clean Integration**\n- Works seamlessly with Django's form validation pipeline\n- Errors are added as non-field errors (via `add_error(None, error)`)\n- Validators run after individual field validation\n- Can coexist with `clean()` method overrides\n\n### 3. **Flexible Validation Functions**\nValidation functions:\n- Receive the form's `cleaned_data` dictionary\n- Can access values of all fields\n- Should raise `ValidationError` if validation fails\n- Support custom error messages\n\n### 4. **Field Existence Checking**\n- Raises `ValueError` with a clear message if referenced fields don't exist\n- Prevents silent failures from misconfigured validators\n\n### 5. **Safe Empty Field Handling**\n- Only validates if all referenced fields are in `cleaned_data`\n- Handles cases where fields might be empty or missing gracefully\n\n### 6. **Inheritance Support**\n- Validators are inherited through form class hierarchies\n- Can be overridden in subclasses\n- Consistent with Django's field inheritance pattern\n\n## Design Decisions\n\n1. **Metaclass Integration**: Used the existing `DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass` rather than creating a new one, keeping the implementation clean and consistent with how fields are handled.\n\n2. **Validation Timing**: Composite validators run after the main `clean()` method, allowing validators to access all cleaned data including any modifications made by `clean()`.\n\n3. **Error Handling**: Errors are added as non-field errors, distinguishing them from individual field errors. This is appropriate since composite validators validate relationships between fields, not individual values.\n\n4. **Decorator Pattern**: Used `@deconstructible` to support Django migrations, making validators serializable.\n\n5. **Backward Compatibility**: All changes are additive:\n   - New file created for validators\n   - Metaclass extended without breaking existing functionality\n   - New validation step added without affecting existing validation steps\n   - No changes to public APIs except addition of new class\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\nWhen test compatibility improves, verify:\n1. Basic composite validation with two fields\n2. Multiple validators on same form\n3. Inheritance of validators across form classes\n4. Error message customization\n5. Missing field handling with clear error messages\n6. Empty/missing field value handling\n7. Integration with Django's validation error types\n8. Deconstructible behavior for migrations\n\n## Requirements Met\n\n\u2705 `CompositeFieldValidator` class exists in Django's forms package\n\u2705 Can be attached to a form class to validate relationships between multiple fields\n\u2705 Accepts a validation function, list of field names to validate, and error message\n\u2705 Integrates with Django's existing form validation pipeline\n\u2705 Raises appropriate Django validation error types\n\u2705 Can be used as a class attribute on form definitions\n\u2705 Handles case where referenced fields don't exist gracefully\n\u2705 Valid Python syntax (verified with py_compile)\n\u2705 Changes limited to `django/forms/`\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/django-code/django/forms/validators.py
"""
Form validators for cross-field validation.
"""

from django.core.exceptions import ValidationError
from django.utils.deconstruct import deconstructible


@deconstructible
class CompositeFieldValidator:
    """
    A validator that validates relationships between multiple form fields.

    This validator allows you to validate that multiple fields satisfy a
    certain condition together. For example, validating that an end_date
    is after a start_date, or that a confirmed_email matches an email field.

    The validator can be attached to a form class as a class attribute
    and will be called during the form's clean() method.

    Example:
        class DateRangeForm(forms.Form):
            start_date = forms.DateField()
            end_date = forms.DateField()

            def validate_date_range(cleaned_data):
                if cleaned_data['end_date'] <= cleaned_data['start_date']:
                    raise ValidationError("End date must be after start date")

            date_range_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(
                validation_function=validate_date_range,
                field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],
                message="End date must be after start date"
            )
    """

    message = "Invalid composite field values."

    def __init__(self, validation_function, field_names, message=None):
        """
        Initialize the CompositeFieldValidator.

        Args:
            validation_function: A callable that takes a dict of cleaned_data
                               and raises ValidationError if validation fails.
            field_names: A list of field names to validate together.
            message: An optional custom error message.
        """
        self.validation_function = validation_function
        sel
... (truncated)

3. EDIT /workspace/django-code/django/forms/forms.py
Before
class DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass(MediaDefiningClass):
    """Collect Fields declared on the base classes."""

    def __new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs):
        # Collect fields from current class and remove them from attrs.
        attrs["declared_fields"] = {
            key: attrs.pop(key)
            for key, value in list(attrs.items())
            if isinstance(value, Field)
        }

        new_class = super().__new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs)

        # Walk through the MRO.
        declared_fields = {}
        for base in reversed(new_class.__mro__):
            # Collect fields from base class.
            if hasattr(base, "declared_fields"):
                declared_fields.update(base.declared_fields)

            # Field shadowing.
            for attr, value in base.__dict__.items():
                if value is None and attr in declared_fields:
                    declared_fields.pop(attr)

        new_class.base_fields = declared_fields
        new_class.declared_fields = declared_fields

        return new_class
After
class DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass(MediaDefiningClass):
    """Collect Fields and CompositeFieldValidators declared on the base classes."""

    def __new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs):
        # Collect fields from current class and remove them from attrs.
        attrs["declared_fields"] = {
            key: attrs.pop(key)
            for key, value in list(attrs.items())
            if isinstance(value, Field)
        }

        # Collect composite field validators from current class and remove them from attrs.
        attrs["declared_composite_validators"] = {
            key: attrs.pop(key)
            for key, value in list(attrs.items())
            if isinstance(value, CompositeFieldValidator)
        }

        new_class = super().__new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs)

        # Walk through the MRO.
        declared_fields = {}
        declared_composite_validators = {}
        for base in reversed(new_class.__mro__):
            # Collect fields from base class.
            if hasattr(base, "declared_fields"):
                declared_fields.update(base.declared_fields)

            # Collect composite validators from base class.
            if hasattr(base, "declared_composite_validators"):
                declared_composite_validators.update(base.declared_composite_validators)

            # Field shadowing.
            for attr, value in base.__dict__.items():
                if value is None and attr in declared_fields:
                    declared_fields.pop(attr)

        new_class.base_fields = declared_fields
        new_class.declared_fields = declared_fields
        new_class.base_composite_validators = declared_composite_validators
        new_class.declared_composite_validators = declared_composite_validators

        return new_class

After
    def _clean_form(self):
        try:
            cleaned_data = self.clean()
        except ValidationError as e:
            self.add_error(None, e)
        else:
            if cleaned_data is not None:
                self.cleaned_data = cleaned_data

    def _clean_composite_validators(self):
        """
        Run all composite field validators for the form.
        """
        for validator in self.declared_composite_validators.values():
            try:
                validator(self)
            except ValidationError as e:
                self.add_error(None, e)

"""
Test script for CompositeFieldValidator implementation.
"""
import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace/django-code')

from django.core.exceptions import ValidationError
from django.forms import Form, CharField, DateField, IntegerField
from django.forms.validators import CompositeFieldValidator

# Test 1: Basic usage with custom validation function
def test_basic_composite_validator():
    """Test basic composite field validator with two fields."""

    def validate_email_match(cleaned_data):
        email = cleaned_data.get('email')
        email_confirm = cleaned_data.get('email_confirm')
        if email and email_confirm and email != email_confirm:
            raise ValidationError("Email fields must match")

    class TestForm(Form):
        email = CharField()
        email_confirm = CharField()

        email_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(
            validation_function=validate_email_match,
            field_names=['email', 'email_confirm'],
            message="Email fields must match"
        )

    # Test with matching emails
    form = TestForm({'email': 'test@example.com', 'email_confirm': 'test@example.com'})
    assert form.is_valid(), f"Form should be valid, got errors: {form.errors}"
    print("✓ Test 1.1 passed: Matching emails")

    # Test with non-matching emails
    form = TestForm({'email': 'test@example.com', 'email_confirm': 'different@example.com'})
    assert not form.is_valid(), "Form should be invalid"
    assert 'email' in form.errors or '__all__' in form.errors, f"Error not in expected location: {form.errors}"
    print("✓ Test 1.2 passed: Non-matching emails detected")

    def _clean_composite_validators(self):
        """
        Run all composite field validators for the form.
        """
        if not hasattr(self, 'declared_composite_validators'):
            return
        for validator in self.declared_composite_validators.values():
            try:
                validator(self)
            except ValidationError as e:
                self.add_error(None, e)

"""

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace/django-code')

try:
    from django.forms.validators import CompositeFieldValidator
    print("✓ Successfully imported CompositeFieldValidator from django.forms.validators")
except ImportError as e:
    print(f"✗ Failed to import CompositeFieldValidator: {e}")
    sys.exit(1)

try:
    from django.forms.forms import DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass
    print("✓ Successfully imported DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass from django.forms.forms")
except ImportError as e:
    print(f"✗ Failed to import DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass: {e}")
    sys.exit(1)

# Check that the metaclass collects composite validators
class TestForm:
    pass

# Manually apply the metaclass to check it works
from django.forms.validators import CompositeFieldValidator

def dummy_validator(cleaned_data):
    pass

class TestFormWithMetaclass(metaclass=DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass):
    validator = CompositeFieldValidator(
        validation_function=dummy_validator,
        field_names=['field1', 'field2']
    )

print(f"✓ Metaclass collected validators: {TestFormWithMetaclass.declared_composite_validators}")
if 'validator' in TestFormWithMetaclass.declared_composite_validators:
    print("✓ Composite validator was successfully collected by metaclass")
else:
    print("✗ Composite validator was not collected by metaclass")
    sys.exit(1)

print("\n✅ All import tests passed!")

14. WRITE /workspace/IMPLEMENTATION_SUMMARY.md
# CompositeFieldValidator Implementation Summary

## Overview
I have successfully implemented the `CompositeFieldValidator` class for Django forms, enabling developers to validate relationships between multiple form fields with a clean, declarative syntax.

## Files Created/Modified

### 1. **django/forms/validators.py** (NEW)
- Created a new module for form validators
- Implemented `CompositeFieldValidator` class with the following features:
  - Accepts a validation function, list of field names, and optional error message
  - Decorated with `@deconstructible` for Django migrations
  - Implements `__call__` to validate form instances
  - Validates that all referenced fields exist
  - Only runs validation when all referenced fields are in cleaned_data
  - Properly handles and re-raises ValidationError
  - Includes `__eq__` and `__repr__` methods for debugging

### 2. **django/forms/forms.py** (MODIFIED)
- **Import**: Added import for `CompositeFieldValidator`
- **DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass**: Extended to collect `CompositeFieldValidator` instances
  - Similar to how it collects `Field` instances
  - Creates `declared_composite_validators` and `base_composite_validators` attributes
  - Supports inheritance of validators across form class hierarchies
- **BaseForm**:
  - Added class attributes: `base_fields`, `base_composite_validators`, `declared_composite_validators`
  - Added `_clean_composite_validators()` method to run validators during form cleaning
  - Integrated into `full_clean()` validation pipeline after `_clean_form()` and before `_post_clean()`

### 3. **django/forms/__init__.py** (MODIFIED)
- Added import of validators module to expose `CompositeFieldValidator` publicly
- Exports via `from django.forms.validators import *`

## How It Works

class_names = [c.name for c in classes]
assert 'CompositeFieldValidator' in class_names, "CompositeFieldValidator class not found"
print("✓ CompositeFieldValidator class exists")

# Check for __init__ method

methods = [node.name for node in cfv_class.body if isinstance(node, ast.FunctionDef)]
assert '__init__' in methods, "__init__ method not found"
assert '__call__' in methods, "__call__ method not found"
assert '__eq__' in methods, "__eq__ method not found"
assert '__repr__' in methods, "__repr__ method not found"

- Exported in django/forms/__init__.py

- Collected by DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass similar to fields

```python
CompositeFieldValidator(
    validation_function,  # Callable that validates cleaned_data
    field_names,          # List of field names to validate
    message=None          # Optional custom error message
)
```

### ✅ Integration with Form Validation Pipeline
1. Validators are collected by metaclass
2. Called in full_clean() method via _clean_composite_validators()
3. Execution order: _clean_fields() → _clean_form() → **_clean_composite_validators()** → _post_clean()
4. Errors added as non-field errors via add_error(None, error)
